Here is how I taught Apollo to hold! Make sure to SAVE this post so you can teach your dog! â˜ºï¸

â€¢Start with an object that your dog would already pick up! (Like a toy) 
â€¢When your dog sniffs or interacts with the toy, either use your clicker or say â€œgoodâ€ or â€œyesâ€ then feed a reward.
â€¢Start to only click/reward when your dog puts their mouth around or on the toy
â€¢Introduce the word â€œholdâ€ once your dog is consistently putting the toy in their mouth 
â€¢Once they understand that â€œholdâ€ means to put their mouth around the toy, start building up the time you want them to hold it for. 
â€¢Once they will hold for a duration of time, you can teach a cue like â€œokayâ€ or â€œdropâ€ when youâ€™re ready for them to release it.
â€¢Once theyâ€™ve mastered that, you can start trying it with different objects!

2021-12-21_17-47-53_UTC.txt
----------

Patience. Distance. Treats. We've got tips to help you better understand anxious dogs and how you can help them feel at ease:

1. Learn about dog body language. Knowing the signs of stress will help you see when a dog is uncomfortable and reduce your risk of pressuring a pup who's not ready for close contact.

2. Keep your distance from anxious dogs and pretend they're not there. Let them observe you from afar and wait for them to make the first move toward you.

3. Treats galore! If you want to befriend an anxious dog, it might help to toss a treat to them without looking. Check for appropriate foods with their owner and whenever you walk by, ignore the pup but toss them a tasty snack. Over time, the dog will learn that you're a cool person that also happens to be a treat dispenser!

4. Patience is key. Some shy dogs, once feeling safe, will become your best buds. Others will be comfortable around you but aloof and that's ok too! With these tips, you'll be set up for success either way.

â¬‡ï¸Comment â€˜WALKSâ€™â¬‡ï¸ to have the links for Better Walks items & training resources sent to your inbox!
 
Tips:
 
1. Dogs are pretty excited when they get out for their walks.  Playing some high energy games can help get some of that energy out so theyâ€™re less likely to pull you.  I like to finish it off with a treat scatter, to help bring the energy level back down to neutral.

2. Dogs move a lot faster than us & have a lot more interest in the environment.  Giving them a long line so they have more space allows them to move around quickly, sniffing & enjoying the environment, without pulling us.

3. I like to use an S-Biner (attached to my fanny pack) so I can be hands free. Who doesnâ€™t like to be hands free?

4. My mind was blown when I found out the @earthrated poop bag dispenser doubled as a poop bag holder.  Again, necessary hands-free miracle.

5. And finally, our magnetic treat pouch.  I used a pull tie one for a long time & bought this one for myself for Christmas & itâ€™s a game changer for when I have gloves onâ€¦ so much easier to quickly access treats!
 
BONUS: Weâ€™re also including some FREE webinars from some qualified trainers to help with everything from loose leash walking to leash reactivity!
 
Make sure you follow @earthrated & @toosmartdogs for more tips to help you and your dog! ğŸ¾

Our furry best friends deserve pampering too! ğŸ˜Š #ad

Taking some time throughout the day to reset, refresh, and recharge can truly make the day better - especially, if we include our dogs in the fun.

â˜€ï¸ Reset: Stop what you're doing and head outside for a nice walk or some patio time. Getting some fresh air and some sun can do a lot for us and our dogs.

ğŸ’¦ Refresh: Take a moment to freshen up (reapply moisturizer, hydrate with some water, etc.) Get your pup cleaned up using some dog wipes and make sure to give them a treat afterwards!

ğŸ”‹ Recharge: Give yourself permission to sit down in a comfortable spot and enjoy a snack, drink, or maybe even a special treat. While you do that, give your dog a tasty chew activity somewhere relaxing as well.

âœ¨ Doing things like this each day/week can further enhance the already awesome bond you have with your pup. ğŸ’š

What are your favorite ways to reset, refresh, and recharge with your dog?

Thanks to @earthrated for all the great products that help us pamper our pups! ğŸ¾

Let dogs be dogs. It may get stinky, it may get dirty, but with @earthrated dog wipes, you can be prepared for less stress and less mess! #ad

I used to catch myself trying to interrupt my dogs from things that would get them dirty. Jade loves to rub up on our privacy trees in our yard, Bruce likes to dig and rub his body on anything stinky, and Freddie really enjoys a good nap in a dirt pile. Recently, I have been making an effort to not try to stop them and instead let them be dogs and get a little dirty. 

Not only is it fun and enriching for the dogs, but it gives me a chance to put our dog wipes to good use and get some training in too.

What ways do your dogs like to get dirty? Let me know in the comments!

â

Info for BONUS TipsğŸ‘‡ğŸ» Save for Later ğŸ¤ğŸ»
 
Recall is an essential skill in my house. We spend the majority of our time off leash in the woods.
 
Building the skills slowly & gradually is so important.  Setting the dogs up for success & staying consistent with rewards is key!
 
Tip 1: Keep it positive & never scold your dog. The last thing you want is for your dog to make the association that reuniting with you is going to make them feel terrible. So keep it positive no matter what!
 
Tip 2: Use a longline! One of the biggest mistakes people make is letting their dog off leash before theyâ€™re ready. If they have the opportunity to practice not listening, itâ€™s more likely to happen again in the future. So keep them on a longline until youâ€™re confident they will be successful.
 
Tip 3: donâ€™t call them when theyâ€™re engaged in the environment, this sets them up for failure. Wait until they finish sniffing & then call them!
 
Bonus tip: always keep a wide variety of rewards on hand. I like to keep single ingredient meat treats & some toys!
 
Toys shown in this video are @earthrated
TUG ğŸ¶
FLY ğŸ•
FETCH ğŸ¾
 
Want MORE recall tips? Check my Story Highlights > Earth Rated ğŸ’š

I also added some links to full webinars & articles for Recall to my LinkTree!

Shining a light on an important occasion like National Adopt a Shelter Dog Month, not only helps raise awareness but also may even encourage people to make room in their hearts for dogs in need. Here at Earth Rated, our team is chock full of people who have experience both fostering and adopting dogs! Because nothing beats advice from people whoâ€™ve done it all before, we asked them for their top tips:â 
â 
- Create a small safe space for the new dog to stay in case they're not comfortable in a crate.â 
â 
- Stock up on the essentials like Poop Bags & Grooming Wipes (remember baths can be stressful)â 
â 
- Offer a mix of soft toys, balls, hard toys, etc to see what interests them the most.â 
â 
- Avoid using any unfamiliar food or treats for the first week.â 
â 
- Try using white noise for stress reduction.â 
â 
- If the new dog is being brought into a new home that already has animals, try keeping the pup in a separate space for the first few hours until all animals can smell each other through the door and adjust to new scents.â 
â 
- Keep in touch with the rescue/shelter in case of emergencies or general questions.

Make Bath Time Less Scary with These 3 Tips: #ad ğŸ› 
 
1) Make the bath/bathroom area cozier with the help of familiar items, like a bed or blanket and their favorite chew.

2) Provide enrichment in or near the bathroom area. You can use things like puzzles and treat dispensing toys filled with some food and treats.

3) Use rewards to help build more positive associations around the area. Depending on your dog's fear, treat them for things like wal  near the bathroom, looking at the tub, and jumping in/out of the tub, etc.

*Bonus Tip* 4) Consider other means of keeping your dog clean, like dog wipes, to help clean them in between baths and while you're training them to overcome their fear. 

â­ï¸ The goal is to help your dog view the bathroom/bath area as a thing where other fun and positive things happen!

#fromdusktilldog #earthrated #earthratedpartner @earthrated #dogtrainingtips #dogtips #doglifestyle #dog101 #dogtraining101 #dogparentslife #dogbaths #dogbehavior

Are you new to this whole Dog Mom/Dog Dad thing? Fear not! Today is National Responsible Dog Ownership Day and while there are no days off when it comes to doing the very best for your dog, weâ€™ve rounded up 7 simple ways to let you know youâ€™re on the right track!â 
â 
Exercise:â 
Your pup needs both physical and mental exercise. Make time for regular walks, games, food puzzles, throwing a ball, etc. Anything to stimulate their mind and body.â 
â 
Veterinary Care:â 
Schedule regular checkups and make sure your dog is up to date on their vaccinations. When in doubt, let your vet check it out!â 
â 
Grooming:â 
From regular coat brushing, nail clipping and tooth brushing, grooming is an important part of pet parenthood. Our hypoallergenic dog wipes are a great option for in-between baths.â 
â 
Training:â 
Set your dog up for success with consistent and positive training. Learning basic commands and a new trick here and there is fun for you and your pup.â 
â 
ID Tags/Microchip:â 
Keeping your dog's tags and microchip up-to-date is invaluable in case you know who decide to make a run for it.â 
â 
Picking Up After Your Dog:â

Love:â

Leash-walking can be a challenge for dogs and owners alike. We asked certified positive reinforcement dog trainer, Sebastien, from Bravo Fido, how you can fix it!

1) Carry a full treat pouch on walks. Be ready to reward your dogâ€™s good behaviour!

2) If your dog pulls, stop! Donâ€™t move, donâ€™t yank, just wait. As soon as your pup stops and looks at you, praise them and give them a treat as a reward.

3) As you walk, if your dog stays by your side, feed them a treat every other step. If he sticks to you for 5 treats in a row, push to every three steps. Keep it up!

Before we get into the nitty gritty â€“ give our awesome partners @earthrated a follow & drop a ğŸ’š in the comments to get added to their close friend list where youâ€™ll get access to more useful info for pet parents & be entered in some exclusive giveaways. 
Â 
Tip #1: Comfort Mat: Why? How?!
A comfort mat is great for helping dogs feel calm & confident. Â Youâ€™ll need a rug, some lavender, yummy food & a calming enrichment toy â€“ the @earthrated CHEW is our pick. Find a quiet spot when you have 3-5 minutes & follow the steps below:
1. Spritz your mat with Lavender & let it settle for 15 minutes. Dogs use their sense of smell to assess situations & pairing the lavender scent can add a layer of familiarity to the rug & the calm feelings.Â 
2. Lay your mat down, sit in front of it & invite your dog to lay on the mat (you can lure them with a high value treat)
3. Give your dog a few treats to reward them for staying on the mat, there is no behaviour requirement, just rewarding for being on the mat.
4. Offer the enrichment item & sit with them. Â I suggest the CHEW, as it allows for an outlet to lick & chew; mastication is a scientifically proven behaviour to better cope with stress!
5. Offer them more treats when they finish.
6. Toss some treats away from the mat, pick the mat up and put it away.
Â 
Tip #2: Cooperative Care is all about having your pet being a willing participant in their required care. Â Check my LinkTree for some resources to get started.
Â 
Tip #3: Provide your pet with some enrichment prior to their appointment; you want them in a relaxed & calm state for their appointment. Â We like to use an enrichment toy like the Earth Rated TREAT, and a quiet walk in the woods.
Â 
Tip #4: Take their comfort mat, treats & their favourite enrichment toy (@earthrated Chew!)
Bonus: if your pet isnâ€™t comfortable with handling, ask your vet if they can get down to your petâ€™s level & limit handling to a minimum.
Â 
Tip #5: Decompression activities are very important after stressful events. Our routine looks similar to Step 3.

In June of 2021, the Canadian government passed legislation to make September 30th a federal statutory holiday called The National Day for Truth and Reconciliation. This day was designed to educate people and promote awareness in Canada about the residential school system and the impact it has had on Indigenous communities for over a centuryâ€”an impact recognized as a cultural genocide, and an impact that continues today.â 
â 
While the province of Quebec (where our office is located) does not currently recognize this day as a statutory holiday, Earth Rated will. We've created a library of books by Indigenous writers for our team, our office will be closed and we will be taking this opportunity to better educate ourselves on this part of Canada's history. We'll be focusing on recognizing our past and how to make progressive steps forward through education and preserving the beautiful land we call home through initiatives like the Pakatakan Project.â 
â 
We hope to see this day recognized by all companies across Canada in the coming years ğŸ§¡

5 WAYS WE USE THE CHEW ğŸ‘‡ğŸ»

1. Stuffed with a chew! It allows the dog to hold it easily and extends chewing time.
2. Stuffed with oversized treats.  This encourages the dog to chew, to break up the pieces to get them out.
3. Peanut butter (or another dog friendly spreadable) smeared inside.  This lasts surprisingly long â€“ about 10 minutes for 1tbsp.
4. Seal one end, stuff with kibble, seal the other end & (optional) freeze!
5. Seal one end, fill with bone broth, seal the other end & freeze.

Versatile, designed with the dog in mind, durable, ergonomic, affordable & dishwasher safe!  Honestly, itâ€™s a home run in my books.

You can grab one & check out the other new @earthrated toys on Amazon & Chewy now at the link in my bio!

Is your dog scared of fireworks? Follow these steps to help soothe your pup! 

1. Give your dog a safe place to go. 

When fear strikes, thereâ€™s nothing like hiding somewhere comforting and familiar. 

Where does your dog feel the safest? If theyâ€™re crate trained, guide them there when fireworks start going off. Do they have a favorite corner? Make sure itâ€™s not blocked off.

2. Be there for them.

Your dogâ€™s favorite â€œsecurity blanketâ€ is you! If you can, being home to reassure your pup will help them feel safer.

The key to keeping your dog calm is to show them a few firecrackers are no big deal. If your dog begins to whimper, gently comfort them and reassure them everything is going to be alright.

3. Play relaxing music.

Sudden loud noises seem scarier among dead silence. Even out the noise level with some relaxing music or TV to avoid jump scares.

Did these tips help? Let us know! 

#earthrated #dogadvice #dogowner #doglife #fireworks

On April 22nd we committed to donating $50,000 to help conserve Canada's natural spaces and wildlife. We want to thank you for helping make it possible for us to support the Pakatakan Project through our partnership with @snapqc 
â 
What is the Pakatakan Project? â 
â 
On the ancestral lands of the Innu communities of Uashat mak Mani-Utenam and Matimekosh-Lac-John, the UAPASHKUSS group identified a series of eight natural sacred sites. The Pakatakan Project advocates for the recognition of these sites as indigenous protected areas to help safeguard Innu cultural and biodiversity heritage for the benefit of all Canadians.â 
â 
The Pakatakan Project Mission:â 
â 
- Protecting places essential to the cultural legacy of the Innus of Uashat mak Mani-Utenam and Matimekosh-Lac-Johnâ 
â 
- Protecting the habitat of 9 at-risk species, including several species sacred to the Innusâ 
â 
- Establishing Indigenous protected areas for local Innu communitiesâ 
â 
We are happy to be able to contribute to the work of this dedicated group who have such a special connection with their land and who are acting as its guardians to ensure its stewardship for generations to come.â  ğŸ§¡â 
â 
To learn more, please visit the link in our bio.

Happy Global Running Day! A day that champions not just the physical health benefits of running but also the mental health benefits it can have. Running with your dog can be a fun activity for you two to do together so we asked certified positive reinforcement dog trainer, Sebastien, from Bravo Fido, for his top tips for running with dogs:â 
â 
- Take it slow. If your dog has never run before, take it easy and build their resistance and stamina over time.â 
â 
- Test out surfaces. If you run in the city, especially on asphalt, check the surface with your bare hand.â 
â 
- Mind the heat. Dogs don't handle heat as well as humans and are at a higher risk for heat stroke.â 
â 
- When nature calls, our Earth Rated dispenser is the perfect running accessory for keeping your poop bags secure.

How much enrichment does your dog need? â¬‡ï¸
 
There is no set amount of enrichment dogs require & it looks different for every dog. Enrichment is about meeting the needs of your individual dog.
 
Sometimes that looks like enrichment toys (like some of the ones you saw in this video).

Sometimes it looks like getting out for a sniff & a dig.

Sometimes it looks like spending quality time with their favourite people or dog friends.

& sometimes it looks like having a quiet place to sleepâ€¦

it can also looks like working on skills required for everyday life (in a stress-free way)!
 
There are so many ways enrichment falls into daily life.
 
What is most important is that you observe your dog, what they thoroughly enjoy & try to offer it to them regularly. 
 
Products in this video are all @earthratedâ€¦
We had their wipes, chew, fetch & treat toys.  All quality products we use on a regular basis & love!

This trick is a lot to fit into one reel, so check out the extra tips below! #EarthRatedPartner

â€œBasketballâ€ is a great example of how mastering the basics can lend itself to really cool tricks! Weâ€™re really just combining these three skills:

ğŸ¾ Retrieve: To teach your dog to retrieve a ball, youâ€™ll need something easy to hold like the Fetch from @earthrated. You can shape the behavior by holding the ball and rewarding when your dog sniffs, touches, nibbles, and finally takes the ball. Transition to holding the ball on the floor and moving it farther away. 

If your dog already loves to fetch, you can toss the ball and reward when they retrieve it. Work up to tossing the ball less until they will take it when stationary. 

ğŸ€ Nose target: Itâ€™s helpful if you dog is familiar with targeting your hand or a disc/stick with your nose. You can use those to bridge to targeting the hoop, or this is a really fun behavior to shape! Sitting behind the hoop and tossing rewards away helps create the motion of going toward the hoop. Reward anything close to touching the hoopâ€”ideally the insideâ€”with their nose, and start rewarding from inside the hoop once they catch on. 

ğŸ˜® Drop it: Ask your dog to drop the ball with your hand right below it, then slowly start moving your hand farther away so your dog learns to target something before dropping the ball. 

Once your dog masters these skills individually, itâ€™s just a matter of stringing them together to create the final trick!

ğŸ’¬ Questions? Drop them in the comments!
